400.perlbench Flags

These are flags that appear in the benchmark sources, categorized as to whether they are portability candidates, mandatory, or forbidden. The descriptions of the pre-existing Perl preprocessor macros are in general taken from src/spec_config.h.

Sections

Selecting one of the following will take you directly to that section:

  • Portability Flags
  • Mandatory Flags
  • Forbidden Flags

    • -DSPEC_CPU_P64
    • [-/]DSPEC_CPU_P64(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This macro specifies that the target system uses the P64 data model; specifically, that integers and longs are 32 bits, while pointers are 64 bits.

    • -DCONSERVATIVE
    • [-/]DCONSERVATIVE(?:=\S*)?\b

    • The opposite of LIBERAL. If this macro is set, some assumptions about how some automatic variables are aligned will not be made. Vector operations and the complement operator may be slower as a result.

    • -DHAS_QUAD

    • -DCASTFLAGS=XXX
    • [-/]DCASTFLAGS(?:=\d*)?\b
    • This symbol contains flags that say what difficulties the compiler has casting odd floating point values to unsigned long. It will be one of
      • 0 = no troubles
      • 1 = couldn't cast < 0
      • 2 = couldn't cast >= 0x80000000
      • 4 = couldn't cast in argument expression list

    • -DNEED_VA_COPY
    • [-/]DNEED_VA_COPY(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This symbol, if defined, indicates that the system stores the variable argument list datatype, va_list, in a format that cannot be copied by simple assignment, so that some other means must be used when copying is required. As such systems vary in their provision (or non-provision) of copying mechanisms, handy.h defines a platform-independent macro, Perl_va_copy(src, dst), to do the job.

    • -DHAS_DUP2
    • [-/]DHAS_DUP2(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This symbol is defined if the dup2 routine is available to duplicate file descriptors. In cases where this is set automatically, it can be disabled by also defining SPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_DUP2.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_DUP2
    • [-/]DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_DUP2(?:=\S*)?\b

    • Prevent HAS_DUP2 from being automatically defined.

    • -DGconvert=XXX
    • -DGconvert=\S+
    • This preprocessor macro is defined to convert a floating point number to a string without a trailing decimal point. This emulates the behavior of sprintf("%g"), but is sometimes much more efficient. If gconvert() is not available, but gcvt() drops the trailing decimal point, then gcvt() is used. If all else fails, a macro using sprintf("%g") is used. Arguments for the Gconvert macro are: value, number of digits, whether trailing zeros should be retained, and the output buffer. The usual values are
      • d_Gconvert='gconvert((x),(n),(t),(b))'
      • d_Gconvert='gcvt((x),(n),(b))'
      • d_Gconvert='sprintf((b),"%.*g",(n),(x))'
      The last two assume trailing zeros should not be kept.
    • -DUid_t_sign=XXX
    • -DUid_t_sign=\S+

    • This symbol holds the signedness of the Uid_t type.

    • -DGid_t_sign=XXX
    • -DGid_t_sign=\S+

    • This symbol holds the signedness of the Gid_t type.

    • -DNV_PRESERVES_UV
    • [-/]DNV_PRESERVES_UV(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This symbol indicates that a variable of type NVTYPE can preserve all the bits of a variable of type UVTYPE. In cases where this is set automatically, it can be disabled by also defining SPEC_CPU_NO_NV_PRESERVES_UV.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_NV_PRESERVES_UV
    • [-/]DSPEC_CPU_NO_NV_PRESERVES_UV(?:=\S*)?\b

    • -DNV_PRESERVES_UV_BITS=XXX
    • -DNV_PRESERVES_UV_BITS=\d+

    • This symbol contains the number of bits a variable of type NVTYPE can preserve of a variable of type UVTYPE.

    • -DSELECT_MIN_BITS=XXX
    • -DSELECT_MIN_BITS=\d+

    • This symbol holds the minimum number of bits operated by select. That is, if you do select(n, ...), how many bits at least will be cleared in the masks if some activity is detected. Usually this is either n or 32*ceil(n/32), especially many little-endians do the latter. This is only useful if you have select(), naturally.

    • -DPERL_PRIfldbl=\S+

    • -DPERL_PRIgldbl=\S+

    • This symbol, if defined, contains the string used by stdio to format long doubles (format 'g') for output.

    • -DPERL_PRIeldbl=XXX
    • -DPERL_PRIeldbl=\S+

    • This symbol, if defined, contains the string used by stdio to format long doubles (format 'e') for output.

    • -DPERL_SCNfldbl=XXX
    • -DPERL_SCNfldbl=\S+

    • This symbol, if defined, contains the string used by stdio to format long doubles (format 'f') for input.

In cases where this is set automatically, it can be disabled by also defining SPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_SIGSETJMP.

    • -DVOIDUSED=XXX
    • -DVOIDUSED=\d+
    • This symbol indicates how much support of the void type is needed. What various bits mean:
      • 1 = supports declaration of void
      • 2 = supports arrays of pointers to functions returning void
      • 4 = supports comparisons between pointers to void functions and addresses of void functions
      • 8 = suports declaration of generic void pointers
    • -DVOIDFLAGS=XXX
    • -DVOIDFLAGS=\d+
    • This symbol indicates how much support of the void type is given by this compiler. What various bits mean:
      • 1 = supports declaration of void
      • 2 = supports arrays of pointers to functions returning void
      • 4 = supports comparisons between pointers to void functions and addresses of void functions
      • 8 = suports declaration of generic void pointers

    • -DBIG_TIME
    • [-/]DBIG_TIME(?:=\S*)?\b

    • If the size of a Time_t is too large to fit into a Perl IV, this define should be set. It will cause time values to be put into an NV.

    • -DBIT_BUCKET=XXX
    • [-/]DBIT_BUCKET(?:=\S*)?

    • This macro should be set to the name of an openable file that will return EOF immediately upon read. On Unix and Unix-like systems, this is "/dev/null". On Windows systems, it is "nul".

    • -DBSD41
    • [-/]DBSD41(?:=\S*)?\b

    • -DBYTEORDER=12345
    • [-/]DBYTEORDER(?:=[0-9xX]*)?

    • This macro indicates the byte order and width of an IV. Possible values are

      • 0x87654321 - Big-endian 64-bit system
      • 0x4321 - Big-endian 32-bit system
      • 0x12345678 - Little-endian 64-bit system
      • 0x1234 - Little-endian 32-bit system
    • -DCLK_TCK=XXX
    • [-/]DCLK_TCK(?:=\d+)?

    • This macro is used in place of HZ if HZ is not defined.

    • -DCODESET=XXX
    • [-/]DCODESET(?:=\S+)?

    • If the nl_langinfo function is available, AND if locales are in use (which would likely cause the benchmark to miscompare), this macro provides the argument to nl_langinfo.

    • -DCYGWIN_WITH_W32API
    • [-/]DCYGWIN_WITH_W32API(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This macro is defined automatically when building under Cygwin with the Win32 API.

    • -DDBL_DIG=XXX
    • [-/]DDBL_DIG(?:=\d*)?\b

    • This flag is used to indicate the number of significant digits in a double precision number. Normally this would be set by the system's "float.h" or "limits.h" header file.

    • -DLDBL_DIG=XXX
    • [-/]DLDBL_DIG(?:=\d*)?\b

    • This flag is used to indicate the number of significant digits in a long double. Normally this would be set by the system's "float.h" or "limits.h" header file.

    • -DLDBL_INFINITY=12345
    • [-/]DLDBL_INFINITY(?i:=[-0-9+efg]*)?\b

    • This flag is used to set the largest value representable in a variable of type long double.

    • [-/]DDBL_INFINITY(?i:=[-0-9+efg]*)?\b

    • This flag is used to set the largest value representable in a variable of type double.

    • [-/]DDBL_MIN(?i:=[-0-9+efg]*)?\b

    • This symbol, if defined, contains the minimum value that can be stored in a variable of type double.

    • -DLDBL_MIN=12345
    • [-/]DLDBL_MIN(?i:=[-0-9+efg]*)?\b

    • This symbol, if defined, contains the minimum value that can be stored in a variable of type long double.

    • This symbol, if defined, contains the maximum value that can be stored in a variable of type double.

    • [-/]DDGUX(?:=\S*)?\b

    • -DDJGPP
    • [-/]DDJGPP(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag indicates that the source is being compiled on an MS-DOS system using the DJGPP development environment. This was not a porting target for CPU2006, so it's unlikely that using this flag will work.

    • -DDONT_DECLARE_STD
    • [-/]DDONT_DECLARE_STD(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag indicates that the source should not provide prototypes for standard functions.

    • -DDOSISH
    • [-/]DDOSISH(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag indicates that the benchmark is being built on a system that is like MS-DOS.

    • -DEBCDIC
    • [-/]DEBCDIC(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag indicates that the benchmark is being built on an EBCDIC system. Good luck with that.

    • -DENV_IS_CASELESS
    • [-/]DENV_IS_CASELESS(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag indicates that environment variable names are not case-sensitive.

    • -DEOF=XXX
    • [-/]DEOF(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag may be used to set the value returned by stdio functions upon encountering an end-of-file condition.

    • -DEPOC
    • [-/]DEPOC(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag indicates that the benchmark is being built on an EPOC system. Good luck with that.

    • -DEXEC_ARGV_CAST=XXX
    • [-/]DEXEC_ARGV_CAST(?:=\S*)?\b

    • If the "argv" argument to exec must be cast to a specific type, this flag may be used to do so.

    • -DFCNTL_CAN_LOCK
    • [-/]DFCNTL_CAN_LOCK(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag should be used if the fcntl() function should be used for file locking.

    • -DFD_CLOEXEC=0, -DFD_CLOEXEC=1
    • [-/]DFD_CLOEXEC=[01]

    • If the close-on-exec flag must or must not be set for open file descriptors before exec()ing, this flag may be used.

    • -DFFLUSH_ALL
    • [-/]DFFLUSH_ALL(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag says that to flush all pending stdio output one must loop through all the stdio file handles and fflush them individually. This flag is ignored if FFLUSH_NULL is defined.

    • -DFILE_base=XXX
    • [-/]DFILE_base(?:=\S*)\b

    • This macro is used to access the _base field (or equivalent) of the FILE structure which is its argument. USE_STDIO_PTR must be defined for this to have any effect.

    • -DFILE_bufsiz=XXX
    • [-/]DFILE_bufsiz(?:=\S*)\b

    • This macro is used to determine the number of bytes in the I/O buffer pointed to by the _base field (or equivalent) of the FILE structure which is its argument. USE_STDIO_PTR must be defined for this to have any effect.

    • -DFILE_cnt=XXX
    • [-/]DFILE_cnt(?:=\S*)\b

    • This macro is used to access the _cnt field (or equivalent) of the FILE structure which is its argument. USE_STDIO_PTR must be defined for this to have any effect.

    • -DFILE_ptr=XXX
    • [-/]DFILE_ptr(?:=\S*)\b

    • This macro is used to access the _ptr field (or equivalent) of the FILE structure which is its argument. USE_STDIO_PTR must be defined for this to have any effect.

    • -DFIXNEGATIVEZERO
    • [-/]DFIXNEGATIVEZERO(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag will cause a number which would stringify as "-0" to be returned as simply "0".

    • -DFSEEKSIZE=XXX
    • [-/]DFSEEKSIZE=\d+\b

    • This flag can be used to specify the size of the return value of fseek() (or fseeko()) in bytes.

    • -DStrerror=XXX
    • [-/]DStrerror(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag may be used to specify the name of the function that performs the equivalent of strerror(), if strerror() is not available on your system.

    • -DStrtol=XXX
    • [-/]DStrtol(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag may be used to specify the name of the function that performs the equivalent of strtol(), if strtol() is not available on your system.

    • -DStrtoul=XXX
    • [-/]DStrtoul(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag may be used to specify the name of the function that performs the equivalent of strtoul(), if strtoul() is not available on your system.

    • -DFflush=XXX
    • [-/]DFflush=\S+\b

    • This flag may be used to specify the name of the function that performs the equivalent of fflush(), if fflush() is not available on your system.

    • -DFpos_t=XXX
    • [-/]DFpos_t=\S+\b

    • This flag can be used to set the type used to declare file positions.

    • -DFree_t=XXX
    • [-/]DFree_t=\S+\b

    • This flag can be used to set the return type of free().

    • -DFstat=XXX
    • [-/]DFstat=\S+\b

    • This flag can be used to define the equivalent of the fstat() function.

    • -DGid_t=XXX
    • [-/]DGid_t=\S+\b

    • This macro holds the return type of getgid() and the type of the argument to setrgid() and related functions.

    • -DGid_t_size=XXX
    • [-/]DGid_t_size=\d+\b

    • Use this flag to set the size of Gid_t in bytes.

    • -DHAS_64K_LIMIT
    • [-/]DHAS_64K_LIMIT(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag should be used on systems which impose a 64KB per-allocation limit.

    • -DHAS_ACCESS
    • [-/]DHAS_ACCESS(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag lets the benchmark know that the access() system call is available to check for accessibility using real UID/GID.

    • -DHAS_ACCESSX
    • [-/]DHAS_ACCESSX(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag lets the benchmark know that the accessx() call is available to do extended access checks.

    • -DHAS_ALARM
    • [-/]DHAS_ALARM(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag lets the benchmark know that the alarm() routine is available.

    • -DHAS_ATOLL
    • [-/]DHAS_ATOLL(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag lets the benchmark know that the atoll() routine is available to convert strings into long longs.

    • -DHAS_BCMP
    • [-/]DHAS_BCMP(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag lets the benchmark know that the bcmp() routine is available to compare blocks of memory.

    • -DHAS_BCOPY
    • [-/]DHAS_BCOPY(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag lets the benchmark know that the bcopy() routine is available to copy blocks of memory.

    • -DHAS_BOOL
    • [-/]DHAS_BOOL(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag indicates that a bool type is available.

    • -DHAS_BZERO
    • [-/]DHAS_BZERO(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag lets the benchmark know that the bzero() routine is available to set a block of memory to 0.

    • -DHAS_DRAND48_PROTOS, -DHAS_DRAND48_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_DRAND48_PROTO, -DHAS_FLOCK_PROTOS, -DHAS_FLOCK_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_FLOCK_PROTO, -DHAS_GETENV_PROTOS, -DHAS_GETENV_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_GETENV_PROTO, -DHAS_GETHOST_PROTOS, -DHAS_GETHOST_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_GETHOST_PROTO, -DHAS_GETNET_PROTOS, -DHAS_GETNET_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_GETNET_PROTO, -DHAS_GETPROTO_PROTOS, -DHAS_GETPROTO_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_GETPROTO_PROTO, -DHAS_GETSERV_PROTOS, -DHAS_GETSERV_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_GETSERV_PROTO, -DHAS_LSEEK_PROTOS, -DHAS_LSEEK_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_LSEEK_PROTO, -DHAS_MODFL_PROTOS, -DHAS_MODFL_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_MODFL_PROTO, -DHAS_REALLOC_PROTOS, -DHAS_REALLOC_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_REALLOC_PROTO, -DHAS_SETRESUID_PROTOS, -DHAS_SETRESUID_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_SETRESUID_PROTO, -DHAS_SETRESGID_PROTOS, -DHAS_SETRESGID_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_SETRESGID_PROTO, -DHAS_SHMAT_PROTOS, -DHAS_SHMAT_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_SHMAT_PROTO, -DHAS_SOCKATMARK_PROTOS, -DHAS_SOCKATMARK_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_SOCKATMARK_PROTO, -DHAS_SYSCALL_PROTOS, -DHAS_SYSCALL_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_SYSCALL_PROTO, -DHAS_TELLDIR_PROTOS, -DHAS_TELLDIR_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_TELLDIR_PROTO, -DHAS_USLEEP_PROTOS, -DHAS_USLEEP_PROTOTYPE, -DHAS_USLEEP_PROTO
    • [-/]DHAS_(DRAND48|FLOCK|GET(?:ENV|HOST|NET|PROTO|SERV)|LSEEK|MODFL|REALLOC|SETRES[UG]ID|SHMAT|SOCKATMARK|SYSCALL|TELLDIR|USLEEP)_PROTO(?:S|TYPE)?\b

    • This flag is used to indicate that a prototype for a function (like drand48(), flock(), etc; there are a large number of such functions) (this should be in lower-case) is available.

    • -DHAS_EACCESS
    • [-/]DHAS_EACCESS(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag lets the benchmark know that the eaccess() call is available to do extended access checks.

    • -DHAS_FLOATINGPOINT_H
    • [-/]DHAS_FLOATINGPOINT_H(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag indicates that the "floatingpoint.h" header file is available.

    • -DHAS_LDBL_SPRINTF_BUG
    • [-/]DHAS_LDBL_SPRINTF_BUG(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This enables code that tries to deal with a bug with Irix/NonStop-UX/PowerUX when calling sprintf with a long double argument.

    • -DHAS_LDBL_SPRINTF_BUG_LESS1
    • [-/]DHAS_LDBL_SPRINTF_BUG_LESS1(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag should be used when the long double sprintf bug affects only values between -1L and 1L. It has no effect unless HAS_LDBL_SPRINTF_BUG is also set.

    • -DHAS_SAFE_BCOPY
    • [-/]DHAS_SAFE_BCOPY(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag indicates that bcopy() can copy overlapping blocks of memory. Normally memcpy() should be used.

    • -DHAS_SAFE_MEMCPY
    • [-/]DHAS_SAFE_MEMCPY(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag indicates that memcpy() can copy overlapping blocks of memory.

    • -DHAS_W32API_WINDOWS_H
    • [-/]DHAS_W32API_WINDOWS_H(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This macro should be set to indicate the presence of "w32api/windows.h" under Cygwin on Windows.

    • Includes:
      • -DCYGWIN_WITH_W32API
    • -DHAS_WAITPID_RUNTIME
    • [-/]DHAS_WAITPID_RUNTIME(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag indicates that the benchmark code should emulate the behavior of waitpid.

    • -DHAS_HTONL, -DHAS_HTONS, -DHAS_HTOVL, -DHAS_HTOVS, -DHAS_HTOHL, -DHAS_HTOHS, -DHAS_VTONL, -DHAS_VTONS, -DHAS_VTOVL, -DHAS_VTOVS, -DHAS_VTOHL, -DHAS_VTOHS, -DHAS_NTONL, -DHAS_NTONS, -DHAS_NTOVL, -DHAS_NTOVS, -DHAS_NTOHL, -DHAS_NTOHS
    • [-/]DHAS_([HVN]TO[NVH][LS])\b

    • This flag is used to indicate that the a function (like htonl(), ntohs(), etc; there are a large number of such functions) (this should be in lower-case) routine is available.

    • -DHAS_FCHDIR, -DHAS_FCHMOD, -DHAS_FSETPOS, -DHAS_FGETPOS, -DHAS_FSEEKO, -DHAS_FTELLO, -DHAS_GETCWD
    • [-/]DHAS_(FCHDIR|FCHMOD|F[SG]ETPOS|FSEEKO|FTELLO|GETCWD)\b

    • This flag is used to indicate that the a function (like fchdir(), fgetpos(), etc; there are a large number of such functions) (this should be in lower-case) routine is available.

    • -DHAS_STRERROR, -DHAS_STRFTIME, -DHAS_STRLCAT, -DHAS_STRLCPY, -DHAS_STRTOLL, -DHAS_STRTOQ, -DHAS_STRTOUL, -DHAS_STRTOULL, -DHAS_STRTOUQ, -DHAS_INDEX
    • [-/]DHAS_(STR(?:ERROR|FTIME|LCAT|LCPY|TOLL|TOQ|TOUL|TOULL|TOUQ)|INDEX)\b

    • This flag is used to indicate that the a function (like strerror(), strftime(), etc; there are a large number of such functions) (this should be in lower-case) routine is available.

    • [-/]DHAS_(LOCALECONV|MSG|NL_LANGINFO|SETLOCALE)\b

    • This flag is used to indicate that the a function (like localeconv(), msg(), etc; there are a large number of such functions) (this should be in lower-case) routine is available.

    • -DHZ=100
    • [-/]DHZ=\d+\b

    • Contains the number of clock ticks in one second. It should be set by a system header file, but in case it's not, you can set it with this flag.

    • -DINT16_MAX=32767, -DINT32_MAX=2147483647, -DINT64_MAX=9223372036854775807
    • [-/]DINT(16|32|64)_MAX=[0-9Ll]+\b

    • This flag can be used to set the largest positive number that can fit in an 16 (or 32 or 64) -bit integer. Its value is not used in all cases.

    • -DINT16_MIN=-32768, -DINT32_MIN=-2147483648, -DINT64_MIN=-9223372036854775808

    • This flag can be used to set the smallest negative number that can fit in an 16 (or 32 or 64) -bit integer. Its value is not used in all cases.

    • This flag can be used to set the largest positive number that can fit in an unsigned 8 (or 16 or 32 or 64) -bit integer. Its value is not used in all cases.

    • -DUINT32_MIN=0, -DUINT64_MIN=0
    • [-/]DUINT(32|64)_MIN=[-0-9Ll]+\b

    • This flag can be used to set the smallest number that can fit in an unsigned 32 (or 64) -bit integer. Its value is not used in all cases.

    • [-/]D(?:UCHAR_MAX|MAXUCHAR)=[0-9lL]*\b

    • [-/]D(?:UINT_MAX|MAXUINT)=[0-9lL]*\b

    • [-/]DMINDOUBLE=(?i:[-0-9efgl]+)\b

    • This flag can be use to indicate to the benchmark the smallest value that is representable by a double.

    • [-/]D(?:SHO?RT_MAX|MAXSHORT)=[-0-9lL]+\b

    • -DI_CRYPT, -DI_FP, -DI_FP_CLASS, -DI_GRP, -DI_IEEEFP, -DI_IEEFP, -DI_LANGINFO, -DI_LIBUTIL, -DI_LOCALE, -DI_MEMORY, -DI_MNTENT, -DI_NDBM, -DI_NETDB, -DI_POLL, -DI_PTHREAD, -DI_PWD, -DI_SFIO, -DI_SHADOW, -DI_SOCKS, -DI_STDDEF, -DI_SUNMATH, -DI_USTAT, -DI_VALUES, -DI_VARARGS

    • These flags are used to set the locale at compilation time. You're allowed to set them, but use of ANY locale other than "C" will almost certainly cause the benchmark to miscompare.

    • -DLOCALE_ENVIRON_REQUIRED

    • This flag indicates that setlocale() requires that at least one of the standard locate environment variables be defined. Using locales will probably break the benchmark, but you're welcome to try anyway.

    • -DMAXPATHLEN=2048, -DPATH_MAX=2048, -D_POSIX_PATH_MAX=2048
    • [-/]D(?:MAXPATHLEN|(?:_POSIX_)?PATH_MAX)(?:=\S*)?\b

    • -DMkdir=XXX
    • [-/]DMkdir=\S+\b

    • This flag can be used to define the equivalent of the mkdir() function.

    • -DStat=XXX
    • [-/]DStat=\S+\b

    • This flag can be used to define the equivalent of the stat() function.

    • -DNO_56_INTERWORK_KLUDGE, -DNO_64_BIT_RAWIO, -DNO_64_BIT_STDIO, -DNO_EFF_ONLY_OK, -DNO_ENVIRON_ARRAY, -DNO_HASH_SEED, -DNO_LOCALE_COLLATE, -DNO_LOCALE_CTYPE, -DNO_LOCALE_NUMERIC, -DNO_NOSUID_CHECK, -DNO_PERL_PRESERVE_IVUV, -DNO_UNARY_PLUS, -DNO_XSLOCKS
    • [-/]DNO_(?:56_INTERWORK_KLUDGE|64_BIT_RAWIO|64_BIT_STDIO|EFF_ONLY_OK|ENVIRON_ARRAY|HASH_SEED|LOCALE_COLLATE|LOCALE_CTYPE|LOCALE_NUMERIC|NOSUID_CHECK|PERL_PRESERVE_IVUV|UNARY_PLUS|XSLOCKS)\b

    • This flag un-does the effect of its non-NO counterpart. These are ALL the defaults, so there's no reason to use one.

    • -DPARAM_NEEDS_TYPES
    • [-/]DPARAM_NEEDS_TYPES(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag can be used if sys/types.h should be included before sys/param.h.

    • -DPERL_FFLUSH_ALL_FOPEN_MAX=XXX, -DFOPEN_MAX=XXX, -DOPEN_MAX=XXX, -D_NFILE=XXX

    • -DPERL_NEED_MY_BETOH16, -DPERL_NEED_MY_BETOH32, -DPERL_NEED_MY_BETOH64, -DPERL_NEED_MY_BETOHI, -DPERL_NEED_MY_BETOHL, -DPERL_NEED_MY_BETOHS, -DPERL_NEED_MY_HTOBE16, -DPERL_NEED_MY_HTOBE32, -DPERL_NEED_MY_HTOBE64, -DPERL_NEED_MY_HTOBEI, -DPERL_NEED_MY_HTOBEL, -DPERL_NEED_MY_HTOBES, -DPERL_NEED_MY_HTOLE16, -DPERL_NEED_MY_HTOLE32, -DPERL_NEED_MY_HTOLE64, -DPERL_NEED_MY_HTOLEI, -DPERL_NEED_MY_HTOLEL, -DPERL_NEED_MY_HTOLES, -DPERL_NEED_MY_LETOH16, -DPERL_NEED_MY_LETOH32, -DPERL_NEED_MY_LETOH64, -DPERL_NEED_MY_LETOHI, -DPERL_NEED_MY_LETOHL, -DPERL_NEED_MY_LETOHS
    • [-/]DPERL_NEED_MY_(BETOH16|BETOH32|BETOH64|BETOHI|BETOHL|BETOHS|HTOBE16|HTOBE32|HTOBE64|HTOBEI|HTOBEL|HTOBES|HTOLE16|HTOLE32|HTOLE64|HTOLEI|HTOLEL|HTOLES|LETOH16|LETOH32|LETOH64|LETOHI|LETOHL|LETOHS)\b

    • [-/]DSTDIO_PTR_LVALUE(?:=\S*)?\b

    • -DSTDIO_PTR_LVAL_NOCHANGE_CNT
    • [-/]DSTDIO_PTR_LVAL_NOCHANGE_CNT(?:=\S*)?\b

    • -DSTDIO_PTR_LVAL_SETS_CNT
    • [-/]DSTDIO_PTR_LVAL_SETS_CNT(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This symbol is defined if using the FILE_ptr macro as an lvalue to increase the pointer by n causes File_cnt(fp) to be decreased by n.

    • -DSYS_NMLN=2048
    • [-/]DSYS_NMLN=\d+\b

    • This flag can be used to set the buffer size for some name length fields on Windows. These fields are probably never used.

    • -DTRUNCATE_U32
    • [-/]DTRUNCATE_U32(?:=\S*)?\b

    • If your system has no integral type of exactly 32 bits, this flag MAY help mitigate the problem. (The benchmark will probably still not work, though.)

    • -DUid_t_size=XXX
    • -DUid_t_size=\d+

    • This symbol holds the number of bytes used by the type specified by Uid_t.

    • -DWNOHANG=1
    • [-/]DWNOHANG(?:=\S*)?\b

    • -D_INTPTR_T_DEFINED
    • [-/]D_INTPTR_T_DEFINED(?:=\S*)?\b

    • Your compiler SHOULD define this symbol if the intptr_t type is available. If the type is available but the symbol is not set, you may avoid a redefinition error by using this flag.

    • -D_UINTPTR_T_DEFINED
    • [-/]D_UINTPTR_T_DEFINED(?:=\S*)?\b

    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_STAT64
    • [-/]DSPEC_CPU_NO_STAT64(?:=\S*)?\b

    • -DTimeval=XXX
    • [-/]DTimeval(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This macro contains the type that should be used when a 'struct timeval' would be called for.

    • -DUid_t=uid_t, -DTime_t=time_t, -DSize_t=size_t, -DMode_t=mode_t
    • [-/]D((?:Uid|Time|Size|Mode)_t)(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag can be used to define what type should be used in place of the standard uid_t (or time_t, size_t, or mode_t) (this should be in lower case).

    • -DSignal_t=XXX
    • [-/]DSignal_t=\S+\b

    • This macro holds the return type of a signal handler.

    • -DMalloc_t=XXX
    • [-/]DMalloc_t=\S+\b

    • This macro holds the return type of malloc() and the type of the argument to free().

    • -DUSE_64_BIT_STDIO, -DUSE_FCNTL64, -DUSE_FGETPOS64, -DUSE_FLOCK64, -DUSE_FOPEN64, -DUSE_FREOPEN64, -DUSE_FSEEK64, -DUSE_FSETPOS64, -DUSE_FSTAT64, -DUSE_FTELL64, -DUSE_FTRUNCATE64, -DUSE_LARGE_FILES, -DUSE_LLSEEK, -DUSE_LSEEK64, -DUSE_LSTAT64, -DUSE_OPEN64, -DUSE_STAT64, -DUSE_TMPFILE64, -DUSE_TRUNCATE64, -DUSE_MORE_BITS, -DUSE_LONG_DOUBLE
    • [-/]DUSE_(?:64_BIT_STDIO|FCNTL64|FGETPOS64|FLOCK64|FOPEN64|FREOPEN64|FSEEK64|FSETPOS64|FSTAT64|FTELL64|FTRUNCATE64|LARGE_FILES|LLSEEK|LSEEK64|LSTAT64|MORE_BITS|OPEN64|STAT64|TMPFILE64|TRUNCATE64|LONG_DOUBLE)\b

    • The benchmark does not use large files or highly precise floating point numbers, but you may use these flags to try it out anyway.

    • -DUSE_LOCALE, -DUSE_LOCALE_COLLATE, -DUSE_LOCALE_CTYPE, -DUSE_LOCALE_NUMERIC
    • [-/]DUSE_LOCALE(?:_COLLATE|_CTYPE|_NUMERIC)?\b

    • Using a locale other than "C" will most likely cause the benchmark to miscompare, but you're still welcome to try.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_CONST64_LL
    • [-/]DSPEC_CPU_CONST64_LL(?:=\S*)?\b

    • If your compiler requires 64-bit integer constants to be noted with an "LL" suffix instead of "i64", use this flag.

Mandatory Flags

  • -DPERL_CORE
  • -I.
  • Iwin32
  • -DWIN32
  • -DPERLDLL
  • -D_CONSOLE
  • -DSPEC_CPU_WINDOWS
    • -DI_FCNTL
    • -DDIRNAMLEN
    • -DI_TIME
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_QUAD
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_FORK

    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_SIGSETJMP
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_SYS_IOCTL
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_UNISTD
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_INTTYPES
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_LONG_LONG
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_INT64_T
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_FCNTL
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_SYS_TIME
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_SYS_TIMES
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_SYS_WAIT
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_TRUNCATE
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_ARPA_INET
    • -DUSE_STAT_RDEV
  • -DSPEC_CPU
    • -DPERL_CORE
    • [-/]DPERL_CORE(?:=\S*)?\b

    • The preprocessor macro PERL_CORE is always defined when building 400.perlbench.

    • -I.
    • -I\.(?=\s|$)

    • The source code for 400.perlbench includes header files in the same directory as the sources.

    • Iwin32
    • [-/]Iwin32(?:=\S*)?\b

    • Windows systems need access to some portability header files contained in the win32 subdirectory when building 400.perlbench.

    • -DWIN32
    • [-/]DWIN32(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag is set when building 400.perlbench on Windows systems.

    • -DPERLDLL
    • [-/]DPERLDLL(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag is set when building 400.perlbench on Windows systems.

    • -D_CONSOLE
    • [-/]D_CONSOLE(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag instructs the compilation system on Windows platforms to generate a non-graphical executable.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_WINDOWS
    • [-/]DSPEC_CPU_WINDOWS(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This macro indicates that the benchmark is being compiled on a Windows system.

    • Includes:
      • -DI_FCNTL
      • -DDIRNAMLEN
      • -DI_TIME
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_QUAD
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_FORK
      • -DHAS_DUP2
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_SIGSETJMP
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_SYS_IOCTL
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_UNISTD
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_INTTYPES
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_LONG_LONG
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_INT64_T
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_FCNTL
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_SYS_TIME
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_SYS_TIMES
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_SYS_WAIT
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAS_TRUNCATE
      • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_I_ARPA_INET
      • -DUSE_STAT_RDEV
    • -DSPEC_CPU
    • [-/]DSPEC_CPU(?:=\S*)?\b

    • This flag indicates that the benchmark is being built with the SPEC CPU2006 harness.
